Default: 0 (not specified).\n208:     int32 container_port = 2;\n209:     // Port number on the host to map the container port to.\n210:     //\n211:     // * Valid host port range is 1-65535.\n212:     // * The value 0 has explicit semantic meaning: it indicates NO host port should be allocated.\n213:     // * The value 0 does NOT indicate dynamic port allocation. Future implementations\n214:     //   of dynamic allocation will use different values/semantics.\n215:     // * Implementations MUST handle the case where this field is explicitly set to 0,\n216:     //   This field SHOULD be omitted when no port is required.\n217:     //\n218:     // Default: If omitted, container port will not be exposed on the host.\n219:     int32 host_port = 3;\n220:     // Host IP.\n221:     string host_ip = 4;\n222: }\n223: \n224: enum MountPropagation {\n225:     // No mount propagation (\"rprivate\" in Linux terminology).\n226:     PROPAGATION_PRIVATE = 0;\n227:     // Mounts get propagated from the host to the container (\"rslave\" in Linux).\n228:     PROPAGATION_HOST_TO_CONTAINER = 1;\n229:     // Mounts get propagated from the host to the container and from the\n230:     // container to the host (\"rshared\" in Linux).\n231:     PROPAGATION_BIDIRECTIONAL = 2;\n232: }\n233: \n234: // Mount specifies a host volume to mount into a container.\n235: message Mount {\n236:     // Path of the mount within the container.\n237:     string container_path = 1;\n238:     // Path of the mount on the host. Has to be empty if the image field below\n239:     // is provided, because those fields are mutually exclusive. If the image\n240:     // field below is nil and the host path doesn't exist, then runtimes should\n241:     // report an error. If the hostpath is a symbolic link, runtimes should\n242:     // follow the symlink and mount the real destination to container.\n243:     string host_path = 2;\n244:     // If set, the mount is read-only.\n245:     bool readonly = 3;\n246:     // If set, the mount needs SELinux relabeling.\n247:     bool selinux_relabel = 4;\n248:     // Requested propagation mode.\n249:     MountPropagation propagation = 5;\n250:     // UidMappings specifies the runtime UID mappings for the mount.\n251:     repeated IDMapping uidMappings = 6;\n252:     // GidMappings specifies the runtime GID mappings for the mount.\n253:     repeated IDMapping gidMappings = 7;\n254:     // If set to true, the mount is made recursive read-only.\n255:     // In this CRI API, recursive_read_only is a plain true/false boolean, although its equivalent\n256:     // in the Kubernetes core API is a quaternary that can be nil, \"Enabled\", \"IfPossible\", or \"Disabled\".\n257:     // kubelet translates that quaternary value in the core API into a boolean in this CRI API.\n258:     // Remarks:\n259:     // - nil is just treated as false\n260:     // - when set to true, readonly must be explicitly set to true, and propagation must be PRIVATE (0).\n261:     // - (readonly == false && recursive_read_only == false) does not make the mount read-only.\n262:     bool recursive_read_only = 8;\n263:     // Mount an image reference (image ID, with or without digest), which is a\n264:     // special use case for image volume mounts. If this field is set, then\n265:     // host_path should be unset. All image mounts are per feature definition\n266:     // readonly (noexec). The kubelet does an PullImage RPC and evaluates the returned\n267:     // PullImageResponse.image_ref value, which is then set to the\n268:     // ImageSpec.image field. Runtimes are expected to mount the image as\n269:     // required.\n270:     // Introduced in the Image Volume Source KEP: https://kep.k8s.io/4639\n271:     ImageSpec image = 9;\n272:     // Specific image sub path to be used from inside the image instead of its\n273:     // root, only necessary if the above image field is set. If the sub path is\n274:     // not empty and does not exist in the image, then runtimes should fail and\n275:     // return an error.\n276:     // Introduced in the Image Volume Source KEP beta graduation: https://kep.k8s.io/4639\n277:     string image_sub_path = 10;\n278: }\n279: \n280: // IDMapping describes host to container ID mappings for a pod sandbox.\n281: message IDMapping {\n282:     // HostId is the id on the host.\n283:     uint32 host_id = 1;\n284:     // ContainerId is the id in the container.\n285:     uint32 container_id = 2;\n286:     // Length is the size of the range to map.\n287:     uint32 length = 3;\n288: }\n289: \n290: // A NamespaceMode describes the intended namespace configuration for each\n291: // of the namespaces (Network, PID, IPC) in NamespaceOption. Runtimes should\n292: // map these modes as appropriate for the technology underlying the runtime.\n293: enum NamespaceMode {\n294:     // A POD namespace is common to all containers in a pod.\n295:     // For example, a container with a PID namespace of POD expects to view\n296:     // all of the processes in all of the containers in the pod.\n297:     POD       = 0;\n298:     // A CONTAINER namespace is restricted to a single container.\n299:     // For example, a container with a PID namespace of CONTAINER expects to\n300:     // view only the processes in that container.\n301:     CONTAINER = 1;\n302:     // A NODE namespace is the namespace of the Kubernetes node.\n303:     // For example, a container with a PID namespace of NODE expects to view\n304:     // all of the processes on the host running the kubelet.\n305:     NODE      = 2;\n306:     // TARGET targets the namespace of another container. When this is specified,\n307:     // a target_id must be specified in NamespaceOption and refer to a container\n308:     // previously created with NamespaceMode CONTAINER. This containers namespace\n309:     // will be made to match that of container target_id.\n310:     // For example, a container with a PID namespace of TARGET expects to view\n311:     // all of the processes that container target_id can view.\n312:     TARGET    = 3;\n313: }\n314: \n315: // UserNamespace describes the intended user namespace configuration for a pod sandbox.\n316: message UserNamespace {\n317:     // Mode is the NamespaceMode for this UserNamespace.\n318:     // Note: NamespaceMode for UserNamespace currently supports only POD and NODE, not CONTAINER OR TARGET.\n319:     NamespaceMode mode = 1;\n320: \n321:     // Uids specifies the UID mappings for the user namespace.\n322:     repeated IDMapping uids = 2;\n323: \n324:     // Gids specifies the GID mappings for the user namespace.\n325:     repeated IDMapping gids = 3;\n326: }\n327: \n328: // NamespaceOption provides options for Linux namespaces.\n329: message NamespaceOption {\n330:     // Network namespace for this container/sandbox.\n331:     // Note: There is currently no way to set CONTAINER scoped network in the Kubernetes API.\n332:     // Namespaces currently set by the kubelet: POD, NODE\n333:     NamespaceMode network = 1;\n334:     // PID namespace for this container/sandbox.\n335:     // Note: The CRI default is POD, but the v1.PodSpec default is CONTAINER.\n336:     // The kubelet's runtime manager will set this to CONTAINER explicitly for v1 pods.\n337:     // Namespaces currently set by the kubelet: POD, CONTAINER, NODE, TARGET\n338:     NamespaceMode pid = 2;\n339:     // IPC namespace for this container/sandbox.\n340:     // Note: There is currently no way to set CONTAINER scoped IPC in the Kubernetes API.\n341:     // Namespaces currently set by the kubelet: POD, NODE\n342:     NamespaceMode ipc = 3;\n343:     // Target Container ID for NamespaceMode of TARGET. This container must have been\n344:     // previously created in the same pod. It is not possible to specify different targets\n345:     // for each namespace.\n346:     string target_id = 4;\n347:     // UsernsOptions for this pod sandbox.\n348:     // The Kubelet picks the user namespace configuration to use for the pod sandbox.  The mappings\n349:     // are specified as part of the UserNamespace struct.  If the struct is nil, then the POD mode\n350:     // must be assumed.  This is done for backward compatibility with older Kubelet versions that\n351:     // do not set a user namespace.\n352:     UserNamespace userns_options = 5;\n353: }\n354: \n355: // SupplementalGroupsPolicy defines how supplemental groups \n356: // of the first container processes are calculated.\n357: enum SupplementalGroupsPolicy {\n358:     // Merge means that the container's provided SupplementalGroups \n359:     // and FsGroup (specified in SecurityContext) will be merged with \n360:     // the primary user's groups as defined in the container image\n361:     // (in /etc/group).\n362:     Merge = 0;\n363:     // Strict means that the container's provided SupplementalGroups\n364:     // and FsGroup (specified in SecurityContext) will be used instead of \n365:     // any groups defined in the container image.\n366:     Strict = 1;\n367: }\n368: \n369: // Int64Value is the wrapper of int64.\n370: message Int64Value {\n371:     // The value.\n372:     int64 value = 1;\n373: }\n374: \n375: // LinuxSandboxSecurityContext holds linux security configuration that will be\n376: // applied to a sandbox. Note that:\n377: // 1) It does not apply to containers in the pods.\n378: // 2) It may not be applicable to a PodSandbox which does not contain any running\n379: //    process.\n380: message LinuxSandboxSecurityContext {\n381:     // Configurations for the sandbox's namespaces.\n382:     // This will be used only if the PodSandbox uses namespace for isolation.\n383:     NamespaceOption namespace_options = 1;\n384:     // Optional SELinux context to be applied.\n385:     SELinuxOption selinux_options = 2;\n386:     // UID to run sandbox processes as, when applicable.\n387:     Int64Value run_as_user = 3;\n388:     // GID to run sandbox processes as, when applicable. run_as_group should only\n389:     // be specified when run_as_user is specified; otherwise, the runtime MUST error.\n390:     Int64Value run_as_group = 8;\n391:     // If set, the root filesystem of the sandbox is read-only.\n392:     bool readonly_rootfs = 4;\n393:     // List of groups applied to the first process run in each container.\n394:     // supplemental_groups_policy can control how groups will be calculated.\n395:     repeated int64 supplemental_groups = 5;\n396:     // supplemental_groups_policy defines how supplemental groups of the first \n397:     // container processes are calculated.\n398:     // Valid values are \"Merge\" and \"Strict\".\n399:     // If not specified, \"Merge\" is used.\n400:     SupplementalGroupsPolicy supplemental_groups_policy = 11;\n401:     // Indicates whether the sandbox will be asked to run a privileged\n402:     // container. If a privileged container is to be executed within it, this\n403:     // MUST be true.\n404:     // This allows a sandbox to take additional security precautions if no\n405:     // privileged containers are expected to be run.\n406:     bool privileged = 6;\n407:     // Seccomp profile for the sandbox.\n408:     SecurityProfile seccomp = 9;\n409:     // AppArmor profile for the sandbox.\n410:     SecurityProfile apparmor = 10;\n411:     // Seccomp profile for the sandbox, candidate values are:\n412:     // * runtime/default: the default profile for the container runtime\n413:     // * unconfined: unconfined profile, ie, no seccomp sandboxing\n414:     // * localhost/<full-path-to-profile>: the profile installed on the node.\n415:     //   <full-path-to-profile> is the full path of the profile.\n416:     // Default: \"\", which is identical with unconfined.\n417:     string seccomp_profile_path = 7 [deprecated=true];\n418: }\n419: \n420: // A security profile which can be used for sandboxes and containers.\n421: message SecurityProfile {\n422:     // Available profile types.\n423:     enum ProfileType {\n424:         // The Default 0 (not specified).\n880:     int64 memory_swap_limit_in_bytes = 10;\n881: }\n882: \n883: // HugepageLimit corresponds to the file`hugetlb.<hugepagesize>.limit_in_byte` in container level cgroup.\n884: // For example, `PageSize=1GB`, `Limit=1073741824` means setting `1073741824` bytes to hugetlb.1GB.limit_in_bytes.\n885: message HugepageLimit {\n886:     // The value of PageSize has uint64 limit = 2;\n892: }\n893: \n894: // SELinuxOption are the labels to be applied to the container.\n895: message SELinuxOption {\n896:     string user = 1;\n897:     string role = 2;\n898:     string type = 3;\n899:     string level = 4;\n900: }\n901: \n902: // Capability contains the container capabilities to add or drop\n903: // Dropping a capability will drop it from all sets.\n904: // If a capability is added to only the add_capabilities list then it gets added to permitted,\n905: // inheritable, effective and bounding sets, i.e. all sets except the ambient set.\n906: // If a capability is added to only the add_ambient_capabilities list then it gets added to all sets, i.e permitted\n907: // inheritable, effective, bounding and ambient sets.\n908: // If a capability is added to add_capabilities and add_ambient_capabilities lists then it gets added to all sets, i.e.\n909: // permitted, inheritable, effective, bounding and ambient sets.\n910: message Capability {\n911:     // List of capabilities to add.\n912:     repeated string add_capabilities = 1;\n913:     // List of capabilities to drop.\n914:     repeated string drop_capabilities = 2;\n915:     // List of ambient capabilities to add.\n916:     repeated string add_ambient_capabilities = 3;\n917: }\n918: \n919: // LinuxContainerSecurityContext holds linux security configuration that will be applied to a container.\n920: message LinuxContainerSecurityContext {\n921:     // Capabilities to add or drop.\n922:     Capability capabilities = 1;\n923:     // If set, run container in privileged mode.\n924:     // Privileged mode is incompatible with the following options. If\n925:     // privileged is set, the following features MAY have no effect:\n926:     // 1. capabilities\n927:     // 2. selinux_options\n928:     // 4. seccomp\n929:     // 5. apparmor\n930:     //\n931:     // Privileged mode implies the following specific options are applied:\n932:     // 1. All capabilities are added.\n933:     // 2. Sensitive paths, such as kernel module paths within sysfs, are not masked.\n934:     // 3. Any sysfs and procfs mounts are mounted RW.\n935:     // 4. AppArmor confinement is not applied.\n936:     // 5. Seccomp restrictions are not applied.\n937:     // 6. The device cgroup does not restrict access to any devices.\n938:     // 7. All devices from the host's /dev are available within the container.\n939:     // 8. SELinux restrictions are not applied (e.g. label=disabled).\n940:     bool privileged = 2;\n941:     // Configurations for the container's namespaces.\n942:     // Only used if the container uses namespace for isolation.\n943:     NamespaceOption namespace_options = 3;\n944:     // SELinux context to be optionally applied.\n945:     SELinuxOption selinux_options = 4;\n946:     // UID to run the container process as. If any required condition is unmet, the node will be not ready.\n1687: // The required conditions include:\n1688: //   * RuntimeReady: RuntimeReady means the runtime is up and ready to accept\n1689: //   basic containers e.g. container only needs host network.\n1690: //   * NetworkReady: NetworkReady means the runtime network is up and ready to\n1691: //   accept containers which require container network.\n1692: // 2. `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/` - Main containerd client and types\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/` - API proto definitions\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/types/` - RunPodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_run.go:53`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RunPodSandboxRequest)\n    (_ *runtime.RunPodSandboxResponse, retErr error)\n```\n- Generates unique sandbox ID\n- Reserves sandbox name to prevent concurrent requests\n- Creates containerd lease for resource tracking\n- Sets up networking via CNI\n- Creates OCI runtime specification\n- Starts sandbox container\n- Hooks for NRI integration\n- Returns sandbox ID on success\n\n**2. StopPodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_stop.go:35`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StopPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StopPodSandboxRequest)\n    (*runtime.StopPodSandboxResponse, error)\n```\n- Finds sandbox by ID\n- Stops all running containers in sandbox (forcibly if needed)\n- Halts sandbox networking\n- Releases network resources\n- Idempotent operation\n\n**3. RemovePodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_remove.go:34`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RemovePodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RemovePodSandboxRequest)\n    (*runtime.RemovePodSandboxResponse, error)\n```\n- Forcibly removes all containers in sandbox\n- Deletes sandbox storage\n- Releases sandbox name reservation\n- Cleans up containerd lease\n- Idempotent operation\n\n#### Container Lifecycle Management\n\n**4. CreateContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_create.go:60`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) CreateContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.CreateContainerRequest)\n    (_ *runtime.CreateContainerResponse, retErr error)\n```\n- Validates sandbox exists\n- Generates container ID and reserves name\n- Creates OCI runtime spec from CRI config\n- Sets up container mounts and volumes\n- Applies resource constraints\n- Creates container in containerd store\n- Returns container ID\n\n**5. StartContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_start.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StartContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StartContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.StartContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Retrieves container from store\n- Verifies sandbox is running\n- Sets up I/O (stdin/stdout/stderr)\n- Starts container task\n- Hooks for NRI integration\n\n**6. StopContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_stop.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StopContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StopContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.StopContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Terminates container task gracefully using timeout\n- Forcibly kills after grace period expires\n- Idempotent operation\n\n**7. RemoveContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_remove.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RemoveContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RemoveContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.RemoveContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Removes container from store\n- Deletes container directory\n- Releases container name reservation\n- Idempotent operation\n\n#### Query Operations\n\n**Status Methods**:\n- `PodSandboxStatus()` (`sandbox_status.go`) - Returns sandbox state, IP, etc.\n- `ContainerStatus()` (`container_status.go`) - Returns container state, resource usage, etc.\n- `ListPodSandbox()` (`sandbox_list.go`) - Filters and lists all sandboxes\n- `ListContainers()` (`container_list.go`) - Filters and lists all containers\n\n#### Streaming Operations\n\n**8. ExecSync** (`container_execsync.go`)\n- Executes command synchronously\n- Captures stdout/stderr\n- Returns exit code\n\n**9. Exec** (`container_exec.go`)\n- Prepares streaming endpoint\n- Returns connection details for kubelet\n- Kubelet establishes streaming connection\n\n**10. Attach** (`container_attach.go`)\n- Prepares streaming endpoint for stdin/stdout/stderr\n- Returns connection details\n\n**11. PortForward** (`sandbox_portforward*.go`)\n- Prepares port forwarding endpoint\n- Platform-specific implementations (Linux, Windows, other)\n\n#### Resource & Configuration Management\n\n**12. UpdateContainerResources** (`container_update_resources*.go`)\n- Updates CPU/memory limits\n- Platform-specific implementations\n\n**13. UpdateRuntimeConfig** (`update_runtime_config*.go`)\n- Updates runtime configuration\n- Modifies pod CIDR or other settings\n\n**14. UpdatePodSandboxResources** (`sandbox_update_resources.go`)\n- Updates pod-level resource constraints\n- Called after kubelet configures cgroups\n\n#### Observability\n\n**15. ContainerStats** (`container_stats.go`)\n- Returns CPU, memory, filesystem usage\n- Uses stats collector\n\n**16. ListContainerStats** (`container_stats_list.go`)\n- Returns stats for multiple containers\n\n**17. PodSandboxStats** (`sandbox_stats*.go`)\n- Returns pod-level statistics\n\n**18. ListPodSandboxStats** (`sandbox_stats_list.go`)\n- Returns stats for multiple sandboxes\n\n**19. `*events.EventMonitor`\n- **Purpose**: Monitors containerd events and converts to CRI events\n- **Usage**: Populates `containerEventsQ` for GetContainerEvents RPC\n\n### Stats Collector\n\n- **Type**: `*StatsCollector`\n- **Purpose**: Collects CPU usage in background\n- **Usage**: Calculates UsageNanoCores for stats queries\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Architecture Summary Diagram\n\n```\nKubernetes Pod\n\n### Step-by-step flow:\n\n1. **kubelet → RunPodSandbox**\n   - CRI server generates sandbox ID\n   - Reserves sandbox name\n   - Calls CNI Setup (allocates IP)\n   - Creates sandbox container via containerd\n   - NRI hook: RunPodSandbox\n   - Returns sandbox ID\n\n2. **kubelet → CreateContainer**\n   - Verifies sandbox exists\n   - Creates container spec\n   - Creates container in containerd store\n   - Container not running yet\n\n3. **kubelet → StartContainer**\n   - Sets up stdin/stdout/stderr\n   - Starts container task\n   - NRI hook: StartContainer\n   - Container begins running\n\n4. **kubelet → ContainerStatus** (polling)\n   - Returns container state, resource usage\n   - kubelet monitors readiness probes\n\n5. **kubelet → StopContainer** (on delete)\n   - Signals SIGTERM\n   - Waits grace period\n   - Kills with SIGKILL\n\n6. **kubelet → RemoveContainer**\n   - Deletes container from store\n   - Releases container name\n\n7. **kubelet → StopPodSandbox**\n   - Stops all containers forcibly\n   - CNI Teardown (releases IP)\n\n8. **kubelet → RemovePodSandbox**\n   - Deletes sandbox from store\n   - Releases sandbox name\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe CRI provides a clean, well-defined gRPC interface that abstracts container runtime specifics from Kubernetes. Containerd's implementation in `internal/cri/server/` is a comprehensive, production-grade realization of this interface that:\n\n1. **Manages lifecycle** of pods and containers with proper state tracking\n2. **Integrates deeply** with Linux kernel features (cgroups, namespaces, CNI)\n3. **Supports extensibility** via NRI for custom resource management\n4. **Provides observability** through metrics, events, and logging\n5. **Ensures reliability** through idempotent operations and proper error handling\n6. **Scales efficiently** using layered storage and concurrent request handling\n\nThe vendoring of containerd types in Kubernetes ensures version compatibility while allowing the CRI specification to evolve independently.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2997,"cache_read_input_tokens":70699,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2997},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b6dcf234-c9dc-4693-a284-8cfc3a5a3463","uuid":"49750563-8245-4010-bbf3-fc03a95725e2"}

RunPodSandbox(context.Context, *RunPodSandboxRequest) (*RunPodSandboxResponse, error)\n    StopPodSandbox(context.Context, *StopPodSandboxRequest) (*StopPodSandboxResponse, error)\n    RemovePodSandbox(context.Context, *RemovePodSandboxRequest) (*RemovePodSandboxResponse, error)\n    // ... (and 29 more methods)\n}\n```\n\n### Key Design Characteristics\n\n1. **Pod Sandbox Lifecycle**: RunPodSandbox → StopPodSandbox → RemovePodSandbox\n2. **Container Lifecycle**: CreateContainer → StartContainer → StopContainer → RemoveContainer\n3. **Query Operations**: PodSandboxStatus, ListPodSandbox, ContainerStatus, ListContainers\n4. **Streaming Operations**: Exec, Attach, PortForward, GetContainerEvents\n5. **Resource Management**: UpdateContainerResources, UpdatePodSandboxResources, UpdateRuntimeConfig\n6. **Observability**: ContainerStats, PodSandboxStats, ListContainerStats, ListPodSandboxStats\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Kubernetes's Vendoring of Containerd\n\nKubernetes vendors containerd's API types to ensure version compatibility:\n\n### Vendored Location\n- **Base**: `vendor/github.com/containerd/`\n- **Subdirectories**:\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/` - Main containerd client and types\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/` - API proto definitions\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/types/` - Core data types\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/containerd/api/services/` - Service definitions\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/errdefs/` - Error definitions\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/log/` - Logging utilities\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/ttrpc/` - Containerd's transport RPC\n  - `vendor/github.com/containerd/typeurl/` - Type URL marshaling\n\n### Vendored API Types\n\n**Core types in `api/types/`**:\n- `descriptor.proto/.pb.go` - OCI image descriptors\n- `mount.proto/.pb.go` - Filesystem mount information\n- `platform.proto/.pb.go` - Hardware platform specification\n- `sandbox.proto/.pb.go` - Sandbox definitions\n- `metrics.proto/.pb.go` - Runtime metrics\n- `event.proto/.pb.go` - Event definitions\n- `introspection.proto/.pb.go` - Server introspection\n\nThis vendoring allows kubelet to interact with containerd through a stable, version-locked API surface.\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Containerd's CRI Implementation\n\n### Implementation Location\n- **Repository**: containerd (mirrored as `github.com/sg-evals/containerd--317286ac`)\n- **Main Implementation Directory**: `internal/cri/server/`\n- **Plugin Entry Point**: `plugins/cri/cri.go`\n\n### Core Service Implementation\n\nThe CRI service is implemented by the `criService` struct located in `internal/cri/server/service.go`:\n\n```go\n// Line 113-166 in service.go\ntype criService struct {\n    runtime.UnimplementedRuntimeServiceServer\n    runtime.UnimplementedImageServiceServer\n\n    RuntimeService  // Dependency for OCI spec loading\n    ImageService    // Dependency for image operations\n\n    // Storage layers\n    sandboxStore      *sandboxstore.Store\n    sandboxNameIndex  *registrar.Registrar\n    containerStore    *containerstore.Store\n    containerNameIndex *registrar.Registrar\n\n    // Networking\n    netPlugin map[string]cni.CNI\n\n    // Containerd client\n    client *containerd.Client\n\n    // Streaming and monitoring\n    streamServer    streaming.Server\n    eventMonitor    *events.EventMonitor\n    containerEventsQ eventq.EventQueue[*runtime.ContainerEventResponse]\n\n    // NRI (Node Resource Interface) integration\n    nri *nri.API\n\n    // Sandbox service for multi-runtime support\n    sandboxService sandboxService\n}\n```\n\n### RPC Method Implementations\n\n#### Pod Sandbox Management\n\n**1. RunPodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_run.go:53`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RunPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RunPodSandboxRequest)\n    (_ *runtime.RunPodSandboxResponse, retErr error)\n```\n- Generates unique sandbox ID\n- Reserves sandbox name to prevent concurrent requests\n- Creates containerd lease for resource tracking\n- Sets up networking via CNI\n- Creates OCI runtime specification\n- Starts sandbox container\n- Hooks for NRI integration\n- Returns sandbox ID on success\n\n**2. StopPodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_stop.go:35`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StopPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StopPodSandboxRequest)\n    (*runtime.StopPodSandboxResponse, error)\n```\n- Finds sandbox by ID\n- Stops all running containers in sandbox (forcibly if needed)\n- Halts sandbox networking\n- Releases network resources\n- Idempotent operation\n\n**3. RemovePodSandbox** (`internal/cri/server/sandbox_remove.go:34`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RemovePodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RemovePodSandboxRequest)\n    (*runtime.RemovePodSandboxResponse, error)\n```\n- Forcibly removes all containers in sandbox\n- Deletes sandbox storage\n- Releases sandbox name reservation\n- Cleans up containerd lease\n- Idempotent operation\n\n#### Container Lifecycle Management\n\n**4. CreateContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_create.go:60`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) CreateContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.CreateContainerRequest)\n    (_ *runtime.CreateContainerResponse, retErr error)\n```\n- Validates sandbox exists\n- Generates container ID and reserves name\n- Creates OCI runtime spec from CRI config\n- Sets up container mounts and volumes\n- Applies resource constraints\n- Creates container in containerd store\n- Returns container ID\n\n**5. StartContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_start.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StartContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StartContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.StartContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Retrieves container from store\n- Verifies sandbox is running\n- Sets up I/O (stdin/stdout/stderr)\n- Starts container task\n- Hooks for NRI integration\n\n**6. StopContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_stop.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) StopContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StopContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.StopContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Terminates container task gracefully using timeout\n- Forcibly kills after grace period expires\n- Idempotent operation\n\n**7. RemoveContainer** (`internal/cri/server/container_remove.go`)\n```go\nfunc (c *criService) RemoveContainer(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.RemoveContainerRequest)\n    (*runtime.RemoveContainerResponse, error)\n```\n- Removes container from store\n- Deletes container directory\n- Releases container name reservation\n- Idempotent operation\n\n#### Query Operations\n\n**Status Methods**:\n- `PodSandboxStatus()` (`sandbox_status.go`) - Returns sandbox state, IP, etc.\n- `ContainerStatus()` (`container_status.go`) - Returns container state, resource usage, etc.\n- `ListPodSandbox()` (`sandbox_list.go`) - Filters and lists all sandboxes\n- `ListContainers()` (`container_list.go`) - Filters and lists all containers\n\n#### Streaming Operations\n\n**8. kubelet\n        |\n        | (gRPC)\n        v\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  CRI Service (api_grpc.pb.go)           │\n│  - RuntimeServiceServer interface       │\n│  - ImageServiceServer interface         │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘\n        |\n        | (implements)\n        v\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  Instrumentation Layer                  │\n│  (logging, tracing, initialization)     │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘\n        |\n        | (wraps)\n        v\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  criService struct (service.go)         │\n│  - Pod lifecycle methods                │\n│  - Container lifecycle methods          │\n│  - Status query methods                 │\n│  - Streaming methods                    │\n│  - Resource management methods          │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘\n        |\n        +──────────────┬──────────────┬────────────────┐\n        |              |              |                |\n        v              v              v                v\n    ┌─────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌─────────────┐ ┌──────────────┐\n    │ Stores  │ │CNI       │ │Containerd   │ │NRI/Events    │\n    │(sandbox)│ │Networks  │ │Client       │ │/Metrics      │\n    └─────────┘ └──────────┘ └─────────────┘ └──────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Lifecycle Example - Running a Pod\n\n### Step-by-step flow:\n\n1. **kubelet → RunPodSandbox**\n   - CRI server generates sandbox ID\n   - Reserves sandbox name\n   - Calls CNI Setup (allocates IP)\n   - Creates sandbox container via containerd\n   - NRI hook: RunPodSandbox\n   - Returns sandbox ID\n\n2. **kubelet → CreateContainer**\n   - Verifies sandbox exists\n   - Creates container spec\n   - Creates container in containerd store\n   - Container not running yet\n\n3. **kubelet → StartContainer**\n   - Sets up stdin/stdout/stderr\n   - Starts container task\n   - NRI hook: StartContainer\n   - Container begins running\n\n4. **kubelet → ContainerStatus** (polling)\n   - Returns container state, resource usage\n   - kubelet monitors readiness probes\n\n5. **kubelet → StopContainer** (on delete)\n   - Signals SIGTERM\n   - Waits grace period\n   - Kills with SIGKILL\n\n6. **kubelet → RemoveContainer**\n   - Deletes container from store\n   - Releases container name\n\n7. **kubelet → StopPodSandbox**\n   - Stops all containers forcibly\n   - CNI Teardown (releases IP)\n\n8. **kubelet → RemovePodSandbox**\n   - Deletes sandbox from store\n   - Releases sandbox name\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe CRI provides a clean, well-defined gRPC interface that abstracts container runtime specifics from Kubernetes. Containerd's implementation in `internal/cri/server/` is a comprehensive, production-grade realization of this interface that:\n\n1. **Manages lifecycle** of pods and containers with proper state tracking\n2. **Integrates deeply** with Linux kernel features (cgroups, namespaces, CNI)\n3. **Supports extensibility** via NRI for custom resource management\n4. **Provides observability** through metrics, events, and logging\n5. **Ensures reliability** through idempotent operations and proper error handling\n6. **Scales efficiently** using layered storage and concurrent request handling\n\nThe vendoring of containerd types in Kubernetes ensures version compatibility while allowing the CRI specification to evolve independently.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
